1.0      Introduction
Cole  Engineering  Group  Ltd.  (Cole  Engineering)  was  retained  by  Decade  Group  Inc.  (the  "Owner")  to  
undertake  a  Traffic  Impact  and  Parking  Study  in  support  of  an  Official  Plan  Amendment,  Rezoning  and 
Site  Plan  application  for  a  mixeduse  redevelopment  on  the  property  municipally  known  as  3100  Keele 
Street, in the North York District  City of Toronto (the "City").   

The subject site is located at the southwest  corner of  Keele Street and Maryport Avenue and is bounded 
by  exiting  single  and  multidwelling  units  to  the  south  and  west,  Maryport  Avenue  to  the  north  and  
Keele  Street  to  the  east.  The  subject  property  is  developed  with  a  Rameses  Shriners  Temple  that  is 
presently  operational  and  will  be  subsequently  demolished.  Access  to  the  site  and  temple  is  presently 
provided via an access driveway off Keele Street and another off Maryport Avenue. Figure 11 illustrates 
the site location.   

The  overall  development  site  area is  approximately  two  (2)  acres.   Currently,  the  property  is  designated 
as  Apartment  Neighbourhood  and  Natural  Area  in  the  City  of  Toronto  Official  Plan.  The  site  is  currently 
zoned  One  Family  Detached  (R5)  in  the  former  City  of  North  York  Zoning  ByLaw  7625,  and  Residential 
Detached  (RD)  in  the  adopted  but  appealed  Harmonized  Zoning  ByLaw  5692013.    The  conceptual 
development  plan  for  the  subject  site  is  a  mixeduse  development  comprised  of  apartment  and 
townhouse units as well as commercial uses. Table 1.1 summarizes the proposed development statistics. 

                                        Table 1.1 ­ Proposed Site Statistics 
                             Use                                                          Size 
                        Apartment                                                      326 units 
                        Townhouse                                                       96 units 
                       Commercial                                                  380 m² (4,090 ft²) 

The  conceptual  site  plan  provides  a  mix  of  commercial  uses  on  the  ground  floor  with  apartment  units 
above.   The  townhouses  are  located  at  the  western  limit  of  the  subject  site  and  are  separated  from  the 
mixeduse  building  by  an  internal  driveway.  Access  to  the  subject  site  is  proposed  via  one  (1)  full 
movement  driveway  off  Maryport  Avenue  connecting  to  an  internal  courtyard.   The  driveway  provides 
one  (1)  lane  in  each  direction  with  outbound  traffic  under  stopcontrol.  Pickup/dropoff  activities  for 
the  mixeduse  and  townhouse  components  will  occur  internally  within  the  courtyard.  Parking  is 
provided  via  three  (3)  levels  of  underground  parking  for  a  total  of  489  parking  spaces.  One  (1)  Type  `G' 
loading  space  is  provided  and  is  located  off  the  internal  courtyard.  Figure  12  illustrates  the  proposed 
site plan.   

The purpose of this study is to: 

         ·   Assess  the  existing  and  future  background  traffic  within  the  study  area  to  identify  any 
             operational  /  safety  concerns  as  well  as  to  identify  any  mitigation  that  may  be  required  to 
             improve operations; 
         ·   Forecast  the  traffic  from  the  proposed  development  and  assign  it  to  the  surrounding  road 
             network  based  on  the  traffic  distribution  assumptions  extracted  from  traffic  impact  studies 
             for background development in proximity to the subject site; 
         ·   Assess  the  impact  of  the  proposed  development  for  a  five  (5)year  (2018)  traffic  horizon  and 
             recommend any improvements required to alleviate any operational / safety concerns; 


TR13-0136 (September 2013)                                                                                      Page 1 of 13
Decade Group Inc.                                                                                             3100 Keele Street
City of Toronto                                                                                Traffic Impact and Parking Study
 
         ·   Review  the  adequacy  of  the  proposed  parking  supply  with  regard  to  the  future  operations  of 
             the site; and, 
         ·   Ensure  sufficient  maneuvering  space  is  provided  in  the  underground  parking  garage  and 
             loading area to minimize onsite circulation conflicts. 

2.0      Study Approach
Existing  traffic  counts  were  obtained  and  conducted  and  a  five  (5)  year  (2018)  horizon  was  selected  to 
represent future traffic conditions, which coincides with the full buildout of the proposed development. 
To  forecast  the  future  (2018)  background  traffic  condition  in  the  vicinity  of  the  subject  site,  an  annual  
growth  rate  is  applied  to  the  study  intersections  to  reflect  and  capture  general  traffic  growth  that  is 
unrelated to new development in the area. In addition to the annual growth rate, there are a number of 
background  developments  in  the  area  that  are  considered  in  the  analysis.  Detailed  calculation 
methodologies and assumptions will be presented in the later chapters. 

Based  on  the  City  approved  Terms  of  Reference  dated  March  27,  2013,  the  study  area  for  this  analysis 
includes the following intersections:  

         ·   Keele Street / Sheppard Avenue West;  
         ·   Keele Street / Diana Street;  
         ·   Keele Street / Whitburn Crescent;  
         ·   Keele Street / Maryport Avenue; and,   
         ·   Maryport Avenue / Site Access.  

Site  traffic  was  derived  using  information  contained  in  the  Trip  Generation,  9th  Edition,  published  by  the 
Institute  of  Transportation  Engineers  (ITE)  and  distributed  based  on  the  traffic  distribution  assumptions 
extracted  from  traffic  impact  studies  for  background  development  in  proximity  to  the  subject  site  and  
on the existing traffic patterns. Future total traffic  consists of future background plus siterelated traffic. 
Traffic analysis is undertaken using Synchro 7 software.  


3.0      Existing Traffic Operation

3.1.     Existing Road Network

The  existing  road  network,  lane  configuration  and  existing  traffic  control  for  the  study  intersections  are 
shown in Figure 31.  The details are described as follows: 

         ·   Keele  Street  is  a  major  northsouth  arterial  road  extending  southwards  from  York  Region  to 
             Bloor Street West in the City of Toronto. Within the study area Keele Street generally has four 
             (4)  through  travel  lanes  with  a  centre  twoway  left  turn  lane  (TWLTL).   Traffic  signal  control  is 
             provided  along  Keele  Street  in  the  site  vicinity  at  Sheppard  Avenue  West,  Diana  Drive  and 
             Whitburn Crescent.  The posted speed limit is 60 km/h.   
         ·   Sheppard  Avenue  West  is  a  major  eastwest  arterial  road  extending  eastwards  from  Weston 
             Road in the City (Etobicoke) to Kingston Road in the City (Scarborough).  Within the study area 
             Sheppard  Avenue  West  generally  has  four  (4)  through  travel  lanes  with  auxiliary  turn  lanes 
             provided at the Keele Street intersection.  The posted speed limit is 60 km/h.   


TR13-0136 (September 2013)                                                                                       Page 2 of 13
 
Decade Group Inc.                                                                                             3100 Keele Street
City of Toronto                                                                                Traffic Impact and Parking Study
 
         ·   Diana  Drive  is  an  eastwest  local  road  which  currently  meets  Keele  Street  as  a  signalized  T
             intersection.  
         ·   Whitburn  Crescent  is  also  an  eastwest  local  road  which  currently  meets  Keele  Street  as  a 
             signalized Tintersection.  
         ·   Maryport  Avenue  is  an  eastwest  local  road  which  currently  meets  Keele  Street  as  an 
             unsignalized Tintersection.  


3.2.     Existing Transit Network

The transit accessibility of the subject site provides excellent opportunity for residents and visitors of the 
development  to  travel  by  transit.    The  subject  site  is  well  served  by  transit  routes  operated  by  the 
Toronto Transit Commission (TTC).  These transit routes include: 

         ·   41  Keele  bus  route  operates  along  Keele  Street  from Keele  Station  to  York  University.   During 
             the  weekday  a.m.  and  p.m.  peak  hour,  it  operates  with  a  headway  of  approximately  five  (5) 
             minutes.    Within  the  study  area,  the  41  Keele  route  has  three  (3)  stops  for  each  direction 
             along Keele Street within a ± one (1) minute walking distance.  
         ·   84  Sheppard  West  bus  route  operates  along  Sheppard  Avenue  West  between  Sheppard
             Yonge  Station  and  Weston  Road,  generally  in  the  eastwest  direction.    During  the  weekday 
             a.m.  and  p.m.  peak  hour,  it  operates  with  an  average  headway  of  approximately  six  (6) 
             minutes.   Within  the  study  area,  the  84  Sheppard  West  bus  route  has  two  (2)  stops  for  each 
             direction  along  Sheppard  Avenue  West  within  a  ±  five  (5)  minute  walking  distance  from  the 
             subject site.  
         ·   106  York  University  bus  route  operates  between  Downsview  Station  and  the  York  University 
             campus, generally in the northsouth direction.  During the weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hour, 
             it  operates  with  an  average  headway  of  approximately  nine  (9)  minutes.    Within  the  study 
             area,  the  106  York  University  bus  route  has  two  (2)  stops  for  each  direction  along  Sheppard 
             Avenue West within a ± five (5) minute walking distance from the subject site.  
         ·   108  Downsview  bus  route  operates  between  Downsview  Station  and  the  Yonge­University 
             Spadina subway, generally in the eastwest direction.  During the weekday a.m. and p.m. peak 
             hour,  it  operates  with  headways  of  approximately  13  minutes  and  17  minutes  respectively.  
             Within  the  study  area,  the  106  York  University  bus  route  has  two  (2)  stops  for  each  direction 
             along Sheppard Avenue West within a ± five (5) minute walking distance from the subject site.  


3.3.     Existing Traffic Data

Existing traffic data were undertaken at the study intersections noted in Section 2.0  by Cole Engineering 
staff,  AccuTraffic  Inc.  on  behalf  of  Cole  Engineering,  and  obtained  from  City  of  Toronto  ­  Traffic  Data 
Centre  &  Safety  Bureau  during  both  weekday  a.m.  (7:00  a.m.9:00  a.m.)  and  p.m.  (4:00  p.m.6:00  p.m.) 
peak  periods.   The  details  of  the  existing  traffic  data  are  presented  in  Table  3.1  and  the  traffic  data  is 
provided in Appendix A.

3.3.1. Existing Traffic Data Adjustment

As  noted  in  Table  3.1,  the  surveyed  traffic  data  was  collected  in  the  previous  calendar  year  (i.e.  year 
2010  and  2011).  Based  on  discussions  with  City  staff,  through  traffic  data  was  balanced  to  the  most 
recent  counts  to  represent  year  2013  volumes.   The  balanced  existing  traffic  volumes  are  illustrated  in 
Figure 32.  

3.4.          Existing Traffic Analysis

The  study  area  intersections  were  analyzed  under  adjusted  existing  traffic  conditions  using  Synchro  7.0 
                                                                           1
software  and  the  City  of  Toronto  Guidelines  for  Using  Synchro  7 .    The  existing  signal  timings  were 
obtained from the City and are reflected in the analysis along with all the existing input parameters.  The 
calculated  Peak  Hour  Factors  (PHF)  were  used  for  the  signalized  intersection  analysis  for  the  weekday 
a.m. peak hour and weekday p.m. peak hour respectively as shown in Table 3.2.  

                                                              Table 3.2 ­ Peak Hour Factor 
                       Intersection                                     AM Peak PHF                      PM Peak PHF 
     Keele Street/ Sheppard Avenue West                                    0.94                                0.91 
            Keele Street / Diana Street                                      0.97                              0.95 
       Keele Street / Whitburn Crescent                                      0.96                              0.94 

The  results  of  the  existing  intersection  operations  are  summarized  in  Table  3.3  with  the  overall  volume 
to  capacity  (v/c)  ratios  and  the  critical  movements  operating  at  v/c  ratios  greater  than  0.85  for  the 
signalized  intersections.    The  signalized  intersection  analysis  under  the  existing  conditions  is 
representative of the following assumptions: 

              ·   The existing lane configurations; 
              ·   The existing signal timing plans; 
              ·   Lane utilization based on Synchro default value; 
              ·   Saturation flow based on Synchro default value of 1,900 pcphpl for all movements; 
              ·   City of Toronto default values for lane widths; 
              ·   Default lost time adjustment values of 1 for peak periods; and, 
              ·   Peak hour factor based on existing traffic count information.

Under  existing  traffic  conditions,  the  signalized  intersections  of  Keele  Street  /  Diana  Street  and  Keele 
Street  /  Whitburn  Crescent  are  currently  operating  with  good  overall  level  of  service  (LOS)  during  the 
weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hour.  Average delays for the intersection of Keele Street / Diana Street are 
2.2  seconds  and  3.0  seconds  for  the  weekday  a.m.  and  p.m.  peak  hour  respectively.   Average  delays  for 
the Keele Street / Whitburn Crescent intersection are 5.0 seconds and 3.2 seconds for the weekday a.m. 
and p.m. peak hour respectively.  

However,  based  on  the  existing  analysis  results,  the  intersection  of  Keele  Street  /  Sheppard  Avenue 
West  is  currently  experiencing  capacity  constraints  during  the  weekday  p.m.  peak  hour  period.    The 
analysis  indicates  that  some  individual  movements  at  this  intersection  are  operating  with  volume  to 
capacity  (v/c)  rations  greater  than  1.0.    Theoretically,  a  maximum  volumecapacity  ratio  for  existing 
conditions  cannot  be  greater  than  1.0.   This  high  v/c  ratio  is  as  a  result  of  conservative  parameters  used 
in Synchro where traffic saturation flow rates through the intersection exceed typical criteria provided in 
the  signal  timing  plan.  While  an  increase  of  saturation  flow  on  the  identified  volumes  would  result  in 
better  capacity,  these  increases  are  not  recommended  for  use  in  planning  or  operational  design  as 
noted  in  the  City  of  Toronto  Guidelines  for  using  Synchro  7.    As  such,  the  above  findings  reflects  a 
conservative analysis. 

Under  existing  traffic  conditions,  the  unsignalized  site  access  intersections  are  operating  at  good  LOS 
with residual capacity during the weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hours. 


4.0      Future (2018) Background Traffic Operation
The  following  sections  outline  the  assumptions  for  the  future  background  traffic  conditions.   It  includes 
existing  traffic  plus  growth  in  traffic  related  to  corridor  growth  and  new  developments  within  the 
immediate area and is based on a five (5)year horizon (year 2018).  Future background assumptions are 
in  accordance  to  the  City  of  Toronto  Traffic  Impact  Study  Guidelines  and  assumptions  as  detailed  in  the 
Terms of Reference discussed with City Staff. 



TR13-0136 (September 2013)                                                                                       Page 5 of 13
 
Decade Group Inc.                                                                                        3100 Keele Street
City of Toronto                                                                           Traffic Impact and Parking Study
 
4.1.     Background Traffic Growth

Future  background  traffic  volumes  for  the  2018  horizon  year  consists  of  the  following  components: 
background  traffic  growth  from  outside  the  study  area  and  trips  generated  by  new  developments  in  the 
vicinity  of  the  study  area.    Based  on  discussion  with  City  staff,  a  0.25%  growth  rate  per  annum  was 
applied  to  all  movements  at  the  Keele  Street  and  Sheppard  Avenue  West  intersection  and  carried 
through along Keele Street to accommodate growth from outside the study area.  

4.2.     Background Development

Based on discussions with City Staff, a total of six (6) background developments located in the vicinity of 
the  subject  site  were  identified  and  recommended  to  be  included  in  our  analysis.    The  identified 
background developments include the following: 

         ·   1055  Wilson  Avenue  (165  dwelling  units  ):  The  trip  generation  and  distribution  for  this 
             development  was  based  on  the  Traffic  Impact  Study  Update  entitled  Brankendale  Investors 
             Inc. prepared by Poulos and Chung Limited dated January 2007.   
         ·   2737 Keele Street,  Phase 2  (200 dwelling units ):  The  Trip generation and distribution for this 
             development  was  based  on  the  Traffic  Impact  Study  entitled  2737  Keele  Street  Phase  2 
             prepared by BA Group dated October 2011.  
         ·   Stanley  Greene  District  Plan  (1336  dwelling  units  and  1,700 m2  retail  space):  The  Trip 
             generation  and  distribution  for  this  development  was  based  on  the  Traffic  Impact  Study 
             entitled Stanley Greene District Plan prepared by BA Group dated July 2011.  
         ·   Humber  River  Regional  Hospital  (309,525 m2  of  institutional  space):  The  Trip  generation  and 
             distribution  for  this  development  was  based  on  the  Traffic  Impact  Study  (Addendum  to 
             Transportation  Assessment,  Highway  401  /  Keele  Street  Provincial  Campus  ­  City  of  Toronto) 
             prepared by Cole Engineering dated February 2009.  
         ·   2800  Keele  Street  (237  dwelling  units):  The  Trip  generation  and  distribution  for  this 
             development  was  based  on  the  Traffic  Impact  Study  entitled  2800  Keele  Street  Residences 
             prepared by Cole Engineering dated October 2012.  
         ·   123  Garratt  Boulevard  (28,039 m2  of  industrial  use):  The  associated  traffic  impact  study  for 
             the  development  entitled  Bombardier  Toronto  Site  Development  was  prepared  by  exp 
             Services Inc. dated October 2012. Based on this study,  the trips associated with the expansion 
             to the existing Bombardier facility in Toronto are likely to occur outside the adjacent roadway 
             peak hour. As such, no trips from the proposed expansion have been included to our analysis.  

The site traffic related to the background developments are provided in Figure 41.   

4.3.     Future (2018) Background Traffic Analysis

Based  on  the  previously  noted  information,  the  balanced  future  (2018)  background  traffic  volumes  are 
illustrated  in  Figure  41.   Future  traffic  volumes  were analyzed  using  Synchro  7.0  software  with  detailed 
calculations  provided  in  Appendix  C.   Table  4.1  summarizes  the  overall  volume  to  capacity  (v/c)  ratios 
and the critical movements operating at v/c ratios greater than 0.85 for the signalized intersections.

Under  future  background  traffic  conditions,  the  signalized  intersections  of  Keele  Street  /  Diana  Street 
and Keele Street / Whitburn Crescent will continue to operate with good overall LOS during the weekday 
a.m.  and  p.m.  peak  hour.    However,  the  intersection  of  Keele  Street  /  Sheppard  Avenue  West  will 
continue  to  operate  with  capacity  constraints  as  is  the  case  in  the existing  traffic  analysis.   This is  due  to 
the  noticeable  increase  in  traffic  generated  from  the identified  background  developments  as well  as  the 
conservative  Synchro  parameters  where  traffic  saturation  flow  rates  through  the  intersection  exceed 
typical criteria provided in the signal timing plan.  

Discussions  with  the City  staff indicate  that  an  advanced  eastbound  leftturn  phase  at  the  Keele  Street  / 
Sheppard Avenue West intersection is planned as part of the Stanley Greene Development. As such, our  
analysis  assumes  the  aforementioned  improvement.  As  summarized  in  Table  4.1,  the  advanced  phase 
results  in  improved  roadway  capacity,  however,  some  movements  in  the  weekday  p.m.  will  continue  to 
experience  capacity  constraints.  Detailed  calculations  for  the  optimized  signal  timing  plan  are  provided 
in Appendix D.  

While  geometric  lane  improvements  would  result  in  better  capacity,  City  staff  indicate  that  such 
improvements  will  only  be  considered  at  a  later  date  when  the  Downsview  Provincial  Campus  is  to 
expand further.  

Under  future  background  traffic,  all  unsignalized  intersections  within  the  study  area  will  continue  to 
operating at acceptable LOS and residual capacity during the weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hours.

5.0      Site Traffic

5.1.     Trip Generation

The  proposed  mixeduse  development  consists  of  a  tower  building  with  a  total  of  326  apartment  units 
and  96  townhouse  units.  Additionally,  commercial  space  with  a  GFA  of  380 m²  (4,090 ft²)  is  proposed  at 
the ground floor of the tower building.   

Trip  generation  for  the  residential  and  commercial  components  of  the  development  was  undertaken 
using  information  contained  in  the  Trip  Generation  Manual,  9th  Edition  published  by  ITE  for  Residential 
Condominium / Townhouse (Land Use Code 230) and Shopping Centre (Land Use Code 820).   

To  recognize  the  multimodal  supportive  environment  in  the  vicinity  of  the  subject  site,  the  information 
on  primary  modes  of  transportation  was  extracted  from  the  2006  Transportation  Tomorrow  Survey 
(TTS)  for  the  subject  site  zone  and  surrounding  zones  with  similar  land  uses  and  characteristics.    A 
review  of  the modal  split  for  the  subject  ward  (Ward  9)  reveals  a  28%  nonauto  split  which  is  applied  to 
the trip generation calculations. 

Passby  for  the  retail  /  commercial  component  of  the  development  were  calculated  based  on  the 
methods  and  averages  described  in  the  ITE  Trip  Generation  Handbook  2nd  Edition.  Table  5.1  summarizes 
the total trip generation for the proposed development. 

                                          Table 5.1 ­ Site Trip Generation

Based  on  the  foregoing,  the  proposed  development  is  expected  to  generate  137  two  (2)way  (24  
inbound  and  113  outbound)  primary  trips  during  the  roadway  a.m.  peak  hour  and  184  two  (2)way  (118 
inbound and 66 outbound) primary trips during the roadway p.m. peak hour.

existing traffic patterns, respectively.  The applied distribution rates are summarized in Table 5.2.

5.3.         Trip Assignment

The proposed site development traffic noted in Section 5.0 assigned to the study are intersections based 
on  the  distribution  rates  presented  in  Section  5.2.  The  projected  site  traffic  volumes  are  illustrated  in 
Figure  51,  Figure  52  and  Figure  53  for  residential  site  trips,  retail  site  trips  and  passby  trips 
respectively.  In  comparison  to  the  increase  in  traffic  as  a  result  of  the  identified  background 
developments,  the  projected  increase  in  road  network  traffic  from  the  proposed  development  is 
negligible.

The  future  total  analysis  reveals  that  the  study  area  signalized  intersections  will  operate  at  capacity 
levels  similar  to  the  future  (2018)  background  scenario.  As  such,  the  impact  of  the  additional 
development  will  not  interfere  with  traffic  operations  of  the  signalized  intersections  within  the  study 
area.  Due  to  the  high  volumes  of  through  traffic  along  Keele  Street,  significant  delays  will  be 
experienced  at  the  Maryport  Avenue  and  Keele  Street  intersection  resulting  in  poor  LOS  for  the 
eastbound  approach.  However,  despite  the  delays,  this  movement  is  expected  to  operate  with  residual 
capacity during weekday a.m. and p.m. peak periods. While signalization of the intersection would result 
in  improved  levels  of  service,  the  projected  traffic  volumes  at  the  Maryport  Avenue  and  Keele  Street 
intersection  do  not  meet  the  signal  warrant  in  Book  12  of  the  Ontario  Traffic  Manual  ­  Traffic  Signals 
(OTM  Book  12).  The  signal  warrant  calculations  are  provided  in  Appendix  F.  The  stop  controlled  site 
access driveway off Maryport Avenue will operate with good LOS, as indicated in Table 6.1.  

On the basis of the future total traffic forecasts, the Keele Street / Sheppard Avenue West intersection is 
expected  to  operate  at  conditions  similar  to  the  future  background  analysis.   It  is  acknowledged  that  a 
number  of  movements  are  forecast  to  operate  with  capacity  constraints,  as  is  the  case  under  future 
background  traffic  conditions.    The  results  of  the  comparison  analyses  between  2018  background  and 
total  conditions  shown  in  Table  6.2  demonstrate  the  minor  cumulative  impact  of  the  site  traffic  relative

7.0       Parking Supply Evaluation
The  proposed  mixeduse  development  consists  of  a  tower  building  with  a  total  of  326  apartment  units 
and  96  townhouse  units,  for  a  total  of  422  units.  Additionally,  commercial  space  with  a  GFA  of  380 m² 
(4,090 ft²)  is  proposed  at  the  ground  floor  of  the  tower  building.  Based  on  the  site  statistics,  a  total  of 
489 parking spaces are proposed via three (3) levels of underground parking.   

The City has recently adopted Harmonized Zoning ByLaw 5692013, which is intended to replace the in
force  bylaws  of  the  former  municipalities  of  the  City. However,  ByLaw  5692013  has  been  appealed  to 
the  Ontario  Municipal  Board.  Therefore,  both  the  former  City  of  North  York  Zoning  ByLaw  7625  and 
Harmonized Zoning ByLaw 5692013 are in effect and constitute applicable law for this site. 

As  the  Harmonized  Zoning  ByLaw  is  newer,  and  represents  the  latest  direction  of  the  City  on  zoning 
provisions,  we  have  used  the  new  Harmonized  Zoning  ByLaw  to  determine  the  adequacy  of  the 
proposed parking supply to service the development proposal.  


TR13-0136 (September 2013)                                                                                       Page 10 of 13
 
Decade Group Inc.                                                                                                           3100 Keele Street
City of Toronto                                                                                              Traffic Impact and Parking Study
 
7.1.          Harmonized Zoning By-Law 569-2013

Table  7.1  summarizes  the  parking  requirements  of  Zoning  ByLaw  5692013,  and  the  proposed  parking 
supply.   

                            Table 7.1 ­ Parking Requirement (City of Toronto ByLaw No. 5692013)2

The proposed parking supply of 489 spaces is sufficient, as it exceeds the requirements under the City of 
Toronto ByLaw No. 5692013 by three (3) spaces.  

7.2.          Loading Requirements

Application  of  the  Harmonized  Zoning  ByLaw  requires  the  proposed  development  to  provide  one  (1) 
Type  `G'  loading  space  and  one  (1)  Type  `C'  loading  space  for  the  residential  component,  and  none  for 
the retail component of the development as it is less than 500 m². In Section 220.5.10.1 (11), the ByLaw 
provides  alternative  options  for  the  Type  `C'  loading space,  being  either  a  Type  `A',  Type  `B',  or  a  second 
Type `G' loading space. 

One (1)  Type `G' loading space is provided. The Harmonized Zoning Bylaw requires one (1) Type `G' and  
one  (1)  Type  `C'  loading  space  for  residential  buildings  with  greater  than  400  units.  However,  as  the 
development  is  only  proposing  422  units  (i.e.  22  units  or  approximately  five  percent  (5%)  above  the 
threshold),  this  loading  space  measuring  13.0 m  by  4.0 m  and  located  in  the  shared  courtyard  will  be 
sufficient  to  accommodate  the  development.  In  order  to  mitigate  any  potential  conflicts,  it  is 
recommended  that  a  schedule  be  set  up  for  the  loading  space  (i.e.  require  a  reservation  prior  to  use)  in 
order to avoid potential overlapping.  




                                        
                                                           
 
2
     Based on all other areas of the City

Decade Group Inc.                                                                                               3100 Keele Street
City of Toronto                                                                                  Traffic Impact and Parking Study
 
7.3.          Bicycle Parking

The  Harmonized  Zoning  ByLaw  requires  the  provision  of  a  minimum  of  317  bicycle  parking  spaces  (287 
longterm  and  30  shortterm)  for  the  apartment  and  townhouse  components.  As  the  commercial 
component of the proposed development is less than 2,000 m², no bicycle parking spaces are required.    

Comparatively,  under  the  Toronto  Green  Standard3,  the  development  is  required  to  provide  a  minimum 
of  321  bicycle  parking  spaces  (289  occupant  and  32  visitors)  for  the  residential  and  commercial 
components of the development.   

The  subject  site  is  proposed  to  include  a  total  of  319  bicycle  parking  spaces  allocated  for  all  uses.   The 
bicycle  parking  spaces  designated  for  occupants  /  long  term  for  all  uses  will  be  distributed  within  the 
underground  parking  levels  (P1)  while  30  visitor  bicycle  parking  spaces  shared  between  all  uses  will  be 
provided  atgrade.  The  proposed  bicycle  parking  provision  is  sufficient  as  it  meets  the  zoning  bylaw 
minimum bicycle parking requirements. 


8.0           Site Access & Operations
To  confirm  the  manoeuvrability  and  accessibility  of  the  loading  space  provided,  the  AutoTURN  program 
using  a  typical  City  of  Toronto  garbage  truck  was  used  to  generate  vehicular  turning  templates.    The 
results  of  the  AutoTURN  analysis  are  provided  in  Figure  71  and  72  for  the  inbound  and  outbound 
movements, respectively.  

An  AutoTURN  analysis  was  undertaken  to  confirm  the  adequacy  of  the  manoeuvring  area  available  in 
the  underground  parking  garage.    Based  on  our  review  of  the  underground  parking  garage  plan,  the 
overall layouts for each level (i.e. P1, P2 and P3) are similar; as such, level P1 was selected for analysis.  A 
typical  full  size  passenger  vehicle  with  a  length  of  5.4 metres  (PTAC)  was  used  to  generate  vehicular 
turning  templates  as  shown  in  Figure  73  and  Figure  74.    From  this  analysis,  it  is  evident  that  the 
proposed  site  plan  provides  functional  parking  spaces  in  all  areas  except  for  four  (4)  parking  spaces  as 
illustrated.  However, suitable access to this space was achieved using a smaller passenger vehicle with a 
length  of  4.5 metres.   As  such,  it  is  recommended  that  these  spots  be  utilized  by  `small  cars'  only  with 
display of appropriate signage. 


9.0           Summary and Conclusions
              ·   The  proposed  development  will  provide  326  apartment  units  and  96  townhouse  units  for  a 
                  total of 422 units. Additionally, 380 m² (4,090 ft²) of ground floor commercial use is proposed.  
              ·   Access  to  the  development  is  proposed  via  an  access  driveway  off  Maryport  Avenue.   It  will 
                  provide  for  twoway  traffic  (one  (1)  lane  per  direction)  with  outbound  traffic  under  stop
                  control. 
              ·   The  development  will  provide  a  total  of  489  vehicular  parking  spaces,  five  (5)  of  which  are 
                  dedicated  for  the  commercial  uses.   This  is  sufficient  to  accommodate  the  development  as  it 
                  exceeds the Zoning ByLaw requirement of 486 spaces.

         ·   The  development  will  provide  a  total  of  319  bicycle  parking  spaces.  This  is  sufficient  to 
             accommodate the development as it meets the existing Zoning ByLaw and the Toronto Green 
             Standards requirements.  
         ·   One  (1)  Type  `G'  loading  space  will  be  provided  and  is  sufficient  to  accommodate  the 
             development. 
         ·   Under existing traffic conditions the signalized intersections of Keele Street / Diana Street and 
             Keele  Street  /  Whitburn  Crescent  are  currently  operating  at  acceptable  levels  of  service  with 
             residual capacity and minimum delay time during the weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hours.  The 
             intersection  of  Keele  Street  /  Sheppard  Avenue  West  is  currently  experiencing  capacity 
             constraints, noticeable delays and vehicular queuing due to heavy traffic volume.   
         ·   Background development traffic and background corridor growth include includes: 
             ­  1055 Wilson Avenue (165 dwelling units ); 
             ­   2737 Keele Street, Phase 2 (200 dwelling units ); 
             ­   Stanley Greene District Plan (1336 dwelling units and 1,700 m2 retail space); 
             ­   Humber River Regional Hospital (309,525 m2 of institutional space); 
             ­   2800 Keele Street (237 dwelling units ); 
             ­   123 Garratt Boulevard (28,039 m2 of industrial use); and,  
             ­   0.25%  corridor  growth  applied  to  the  all  traffic  volume  at  the  intersection  of  Keele  Street 
                 and Sheppard Avenue West over a five (5) year horizon. 
         ·   The  subject  development  will  generate  137  and  184  gross  twoway  vehicular  trips  during  the 
             weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hours, respectively.   
         ·   Under  the  future  total  traffic  conditions  the  signalized  intersections  of  Keele  Street  /  Diana 
             Street  and  Keele  Street  /  Whitburn  Crescent  will  continue  to  operate  at  acceptable  levels  of 
             service  during  the  weekday  a.m.  and  p.m.  peak  hour.    The  intersection  of  Keele  Street  / 
             Sheppard  Avenue  West  will  continue  to  operate  with  capacity  constraints  and  delays  similar 
             to  the  future  background  conditions.  Due  to  the  high  volumes  of  through  traffic  along  Keele 
             Street,  significant  delays  will  be  experienced  at  the  Maryport  Avenue  and  Keele  Street 
             intersection resulting in poor levels of service at the eastbound movements. However, despite 
             the  delays,  this  movement  is  expected  to  operate  with  residual  capacity  during  weekday  a.m. 
             and  p.m.  peak  periods  Further,  the  proposed  unsignalized  access  driveway  off  Maryport 
             Avenue  will  operate  at  good  levels  of  service  with  residual  capacity.    Overall,  the  adjacent 
             road network is sufficient to accommodate the minimum increase in site traffic volume.

Statement Of Limiting Conditions And Assumptions 
                                                 
                 Statement of Limiting Conditions and Assumptions

1.   This Report/Study (the "Work") has been prepared at the request of, and for the exclusive use of, the Owner, and its
     affiliates (the "Intended Users"). No one other than the Intended Users has the right to use and rely on the Work without
     first obtaining the written authorization of Cole Engineering Group Ltd. (Cole Engineering) and its Owner.
2.   Cole Engineering expressly excludes liability to any party except the Intended Users for any use of, and/or reliance upon,
     the Work.
3.   Cole Engineering notes that the following assumptions were made in completing the Work:
     a)   the land use description(s) supplied to us are correct;
     b)   the surveys and data supplied to Cole Engineering by the Owner are accurate;
     c)   market timing, approval delivery and secondary source information is within the control of Parties other than Cole
          Engineering; and
     d)   there are no encroachments, leases, covenants, binding agreements, restrictions, pledges, charges, liens or special
          assessments outstanding, or encumbrances which would significantly affect the use or servicing.

     Investigations have not been carried out to verify these assumptions. Cole Engineering deems the sources of data and
     statistical information contained herein to be reliable, but we extend no guarantee of accuracy in these respects.

4.   Cole Engineering accepts no responsibility for legal interpretations, questions of survey, opinion of title, hidden or
     inconspicuous conditions of the property, toxic wastes or contaminated materials, soil or sub-soil conditions, environmental,
     engineering or other factual and technical matters disclosed by the Owner, the Client, or any public agency, which by their
     nature, may change the outcome of the Work. Such factors, beyond the scope of this Work, could affect the findings,
     conclusions and opinions rendered in the Work. We have made disclosure of related potential problems that have come to
     our attention. Responsibility for diligence with respect to all matters of fact reported herein rests with the Intended Users.
5.   Cole Engineering practices engineering in the general areas of infrastructure and transportation. It is not qualified to and is
     not providing legal or planning advice in this Work.
6.   The legal description of the property and the area of the site were based upon surveys and data supplied to us by the Owner.
     The plans, photographs, and sketches contained in this report are included solely to aide in visualizing the location of the
     property, the configuration and boundaries of the site, and the relative position of the improvements on the said lands.
7.   We have made investigations from secondary sources as documented in the Work, but we have not checked for compliance
     with by-laws, codes, agency and governmental regulations, etc., unless specifically noted in the Work.
8.   Because conditions, including capacity, allocation, economic, social, and political factors change rapidly and, on occasion,
     without notice or warning, the findings of the Work expressed herein, are as of the date of the Work and cannot necessarily
     be relied upon as of any other date without subsequent advice from Cole Engineering.
9.   The value of proposed improvements should be applied only with regard to the purpose and function of the Work, as
     outlined in the body of this Work. Any cost estimates set out in the Work are based on construction averages and subject to
     change.
10. Neither possession of the Work, nor a copy of it, carries the right of publication. All copyright in the Work is reserved to
    Cole Engineering. The Work shall not be disclosed, produced or reproduced, quoted from, or referred to, in whole or in
    part, or published in any manner, without the express written consent of Cole Engineering and the Owner.
11. The Work is only valid if it bears the professional engineer's seal and original signature of the author, and if considered in
    its entirety. Responsibility for unauthorized alteration to the Work is denied.
